<div id="review_1684581034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1684581034" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684581034?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684581034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9537820256129842084"><i>“The time is now. They are coming,” Isaiah said, drifting back into dreams, his last word barely a whisper: “Diviners.”</i><br/><br/>This was exactly my kind of book - with talk about the occult, magical-realism, and even a little horror (that I could handle for once) - I couldn’t help but fall for <b>The Diviners</b>. <a href='http://maggie-stiefvater.tumblr.com/post/146764323796/hey-maggie-i-was-just-wondering-if-you-have-any' rel='nofollow noopener'>To quote Maggie Stiefvater</a>, good magic is a little horrific, and good horror is always a little magical. And Libba Bray brought just that to the table with this chilling and wondrous book.<br/><br/>This follows</span>
  <span id="freeText9537820256129842084" style="display:none"><i>“The time is now. They are coming,” Isaiah said, drifting back into dreams, his last word barely a whisper: “Diviners.”</i><br><br>This was exactly my kind of book - with talk about the occult, magical-realism, and even a little horror (that I could handle for once) - I couldn’t help but fall for <b>The Diviners</b>. <a href="http://maggie-stiefvater.tumblr.com/post/146764323796/hey-maggie-i-was-just-wondering-if-you-have-any" rel="nofollow noopener">To quote Maggie Stiefvater</a>, good magic is a little horrific, and good horror is always a little magical. And Libba Bray brought just that to the table with this chilling and wondrous book.<br><br>This follows the tale of seventeen-year-old Evangeline (Evie) O’Neill, who gets send to New York for a few months to stay with her uncle Will after an unfortunate incident involving a louse and a lothario named Harold Brodie. An incident she, rightfully, is not willing to apoligze for because that would mean explaining what happened.<br><br>You see, Evie has special powers— she can tell your secrets simply by holding an object dear to you and concentrating on it. But the aftereffects of her object reading can leave her feeling woozy and sick.<br><br><i>“In New York, she could reinvent herself. She could be somebody.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713698.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713699.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br>When Evie arrives in New York after having lived in boring old Zenith, Ohio— it’s certainly a step-up for her. It’s thrilling, unnerving, and enlightening.<br><br>Speaking of unnerving, Sam Lloyd was introduced when Evie stepped of the train, and I was completely swept off my feet. I mean, I had stars in my eyes and everything…<br><br>To be frank, I went into this knowing I’d be completely smitten with Sam Lloyd because I saw some beautiful fanart (by one of my favorite artists)— and I was certainly not disappointed with his first appearance in the book.<br><br><i>“You can’t blame a fella for kissing the prettiest girl in New York, can you, sister?” Sam’s grin was anything but apologetic.<br>Evie brought up her knee quickly and decisively, and he dropped to the floor like a grain sack. “You can’t blame a girl for her quick reflexes now, can you, pal?”</i><br><br>And I still can’t believe he pick-pocketed her. I mean, I knew he was trouble when he opened his mouth, but I hadn’t guessed what sort of trouble.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468496887i/19713700._SY540_.png" width="445" height="655" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><a href="http://xla-hainex.tumblr.com/post/146719739244/my-beautiful-little-fox-sam-lloyd-from-diviners-by" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a><br><br><i>“Thick, dark hair with a longer piece in front that refused to stay swept back. Amber eyes and dark brows. His smile could only be described as wolfish.”</i><br>(She just captured his smile perfectly. Sam Lloyd was painted by the brushstrokes of angels.)<br><br>And by then Evie finally arrives at the good old Bennington with her friend Mabel Rose, where they both encounter Theta Knight—a glamorous Ziegfeld girl.<br><br><i>“Evie decided she liked Theta. It was hard not to be taken by her glamour. She’d never known anyone in Ohio who lived on her own terms, wore silk men’s pajamas into a public lobby, and could toss a dozen roses like they were a cup of Automat coffee.”</i><br><br>It’s 1926, and New York is filled with speakeasies, Ziegfeld girls, and rakish pickpockets. The only catch is that living with her uncle Will and his unhealthy obsession with the occult means having to risk her supernatural secret being discovered.<br><br>I actually found Will's obsession with the mystical so damn interesting. His lectures never felt boring or tedious because they informed me of so much.<br><br><i>“Will smiled as the boys chuckled. “And yet, there are mysteries. How does one explain the stories of people who exhibit unusual powers?”<br>Evie felt a tingle down her spine.<br>“Powers?” a boy repeated in a skeptical tone bordering on contempt.<br>“People who claim to be able to speak to the dead, such as psychics or spiritual mediums. People who say they have been healed by the laying on of hands. Who can see glimpses of the future or know a card before it is played. The early records of the Americas talk of Indian spirit walkers. The Puritans knew of cunning folk. And during the American Revolution, Benjamin Franklin wrote of prophetic dreams that influenced the course of the war and shaped the nation. What do you say to that?”</i><br><br>But when the police find a murdered girl (Ruta Badowski) branded with a cryptic symbol and Will is called to the scene, Evie realizes her gift could help catch a serial killer.<br><br><i>“Ruta was only nineteen years old, and what she knew most was want—a constant longing for the good life she saw all around her.”</i><br><br>Getting into Ruta's head while this unspeakably horrendous act happened at the hands of John 'Naughty John' Hobbes, broke a piece of my heart.<br><br><i>“Naughty John, Naughty John, does his work with his apron on. Cuts your throat and takes your bones, sells ’em off for a coupla stones.”</i><br><br>Mr. Hobbes and his cold blue eyes gave me nightmares. And like Evie and her uncle said:<br><br><i>“He’s a monster,” Evie said. “Isn’t he?”<br>Will reached into a bowl of bridge mix. He juggled the candies in his hand without eating them. “Indeed. But that’s a what, not a why. Nothing is done without purpose, however twisted that purpose may be.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713701.gif" width="540" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As Evie jumps headlong into a dance with a murderer, other stories unfold in the city that never sleeps.<br>And we circle between the lives of a few quaint people:<br><br>A young man named Memphis is caught between two worlds.<br><br><i>“I just need a change of luck is all.”<br>“Don’t we all,” Memphis said and moved on.”</i><br><br>A chorus girl named Theta who's running from her past.<br><br><i>“Theta.” Evie waved a finger in Theta’s general direction. “You didn’t let me tell your secrets.”<br>Theta wavered for a minute, but she was too drunk to say no. “Here ya go, Evil,” she said, passing over an onyx bracelet shaped like a jaguar. “My birthday is February twenty-third, and I had one of those limp sandwiches in the kitchen for dinner a million hours ago.”<br>Evie squeezed the bracelet and felt an overpowering sensation of sadness, and a trace of fear. She saw Theta running in the dead of night, her dress torn and her face a wreck. Theta was afraid, so very afraid.”</i><br><br>A student named Jericho hides a shocking secret.<br><br><i>“You asked me about how I came to live with your uncle Will. I didn’t answer you right away,” Jericho started. He pulled a heel of bread from his pocket and unwrapped it.<br>“No, you didn’t,” Evie said. Once, she’d been very curious about that. She couldn’t see that it mattered now, with her expulsion imminent. But she was grateful to Jericho for coming after her, for trying to comfort her in his way. She just wanted him to keep talking. “Will you tell me now?”</i><br>YES!! After he told Evie his secrets, so much of his past conversations made sense (particularly the one with Marlowe).<br><br><i>“I told myself a hundred lies. Children do that. It’s amazing the sorts of things you’ll make yourself believe.”</i><br><br>But I will admit that I was a little suspicious of Jericho because his childhood sounded a little similar to Naughty John's story:<br><br><i>“Naughty John, born John Hobbes, raised in Brooklyn, New York, at the Mother Nova Orphanage, where he was left at the age of nine. A troubled youth, he ran away twice, finally succeeding when he was fifteen.”</i><br>(They were both at the age of nine when they were left at an Orphanage.)<br><br>But as always, I was getting way over my head. And that's also the reason why I don't read that much mystery— I suck at solving it.<br><br>And my favorite, Sam Lloyd, juggling his ordeals to make it in New York as a self-made man.<br><br><i>“Sam, too, would make his fortune, and then he’d find the place in the postcard. He’d find her.”</i><br><br>He was one of the most interesting characters to read about. The mystery behind his actions made me anticipate his every move.<br><br><i>“This job at the museum had been a stroke of good luck, easier than hustling magic tricks on the streets of Times Square. All he had to do was hold on for a little while—long enough to find out who needed to pay for what had happened to his family. And they would pay.”</i><br><br>And that job at the museum was pretty great for my entertainment— his banter with Evie made my cheeks hurt from smiling so damn much.<br><br><i>“Absence makes the heart grow fonder. Let’s put that phrase to the test, shall we? I’ll get your hat.”<br>“No can do. Your uncle needs my help. Look at all this stuff—who knew there were so many superstitious charms? Like this—love charm of the Hopi. Oh, I better not let you hold this, sister. You might get goofy for me.”<br>“That’ll be the day.”<br>“I’m counting on that day.”<br>“I hope you can count pretty high, then,” Evie said.”</i><br>I knew <b>I</b> was getting pretty goofy for him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713702.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713703.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and I also have to mention Evie's dreams because they were one of the most fascinating parts of this book.<br>Especially this next one she had while in the collections room:<br><br><i>“Shadow people. She’d turn her head just in time to see them retreat into the growing gloom. Whispering, “She’s one. She’s one of them. You can’t stop us. Nothing can stop us.”<br>Evie turned a corner and was surprised to see Henry also walking the streets, as if looking for someone. His eyes widened when he saw her. “Evie, what are you doing here? Don’t remember me,” he said, and when she looked again, he was gone. ”</i><br><br>It gave me chills because I was kind of terrified. And then Sam wakes her from her nightmare and manages to make <s>me</s> her laugh after seeing such horrors:<br><br><i>“This fella asked for your uncle, but I told him you were in charge, Your Highness.” Sam returned the bow.<br>Evie replied with an eye-roll. “Do you think you can manage to not steal anything while I’m gone?”<br>“The only thing I’m trying to steal is your heart, doll.” Sam smirked.<br>“You’re not that talented a thief, Sam Lloyd.”</i><br><br>Also, the love he had for his mother added like 10 extra points in my book:<br><br><i>“I thought you said she died.”<br>“That’s what they told us. Two years ago, I got this.” He pulled the worn postcard of trees and mountains from his pocket. Evie pretended it was the first time she’d seen it.<br>“Pretty. Where is this?”<br>“I don’t know. That phrase on the back, there. It’s Russian.”<br>Evie examined the soft handwriting, obviously feminine.<br>“It means ‘little fox.’ It was my mother’s nickname for me. She was the only one who ever called me that. That’s when I knew my mother was alive, and I was going to find her. So I took off. I joined up with the navy for a bit—till they found out I was only fifteen. Then I fell in with a circus.”</i><br>Like I said, <b>Sam Lloyd has a piece of my heart</b>.<br><br>Okay, so I was fully rooting for Sam and Evie to get together— but then Jericho realises somewhere along the road that he's into Evie? And I’m just… WHAT??<br><br><i>“Jericho didn’t know if he would function like a normal man. He only knew that he had all the feelings of one. He wanted Evie. He wanted her desperately. With his hands on hers, he imagined what it would be like to kiss her, to make love to her. She was a little spoiled and often selfish, a good-time girl with a surprising kind streak. She ran toward life full tilt while Jericho held back, not daring. She made him feel alive, and he wanted more of it.”</i><br><br>I was unsettled, too, by the feelings she had developed for him.<br><br><i>“Are you feeling all right, Jericho?” Evie asked a bit shyly. “Can I get you anything?”<br>“No, I’m… jake, thanks,” he said, trying out the word with a smile.<br>Sam watched the two of them from the sidelines. Something had happened up in Brethren beyond their finding the pendant and escaping from the new faithful. And Sam didn’t like it.”</i><br>Right there with you, Sam.<br><br>I’m not saying that Evie <b>should</b> be with Sam, just that her sudden infatuation with Jericho wasn't to my liking (especially when you put Mabel in the picture).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713704.gif" width="247" height="247" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713705.gif" width="247" height="247" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But if you put that aside, just about everything was written so magically and with such a chilling atmosphere. There were so many moments that I loved, especially the ones where all the characters were in the same place.<br><br>I mean, when I got to see Memphis and Theta interact (among many other happenings), it made my heart soar.<br><br><i>“Poet, we’ve gotta scram!”<br>Memphis ran with Theta around a corner, where he pulled her into a telephone booth. She looked up through heavy lashes into Memphis’s handsome face. She’d seen plenty of handsome fellas before, but none who wrote poetry and shared the same strange nightmare.”</i><br><br>The fact that they shared the same nightmare was mind-boggling, I'm still in awe.<br><br><i>“Papa Charles isn’t gonna like this,” Memphis said. “He pays the cops enough not to raid his clubs. I hope your friends got out all right.”<br>“Me, too,” Theta said. She still held Evie’s handbag. “I suppose I’d better blow home and see if they did.”<br>Memphis felt his heart sink. He didn’t want the evening to end. “I could take you for a cup of coffee first, if you like. I know I could sure use one.”<br>Theta smiled. It was a sweet smile, almost shy. “Thanks, Poet. But I should get my beauty sleep.”<br>Memphis started to say something clever—“Why? You’re already the best-looking girl in town”—but didn’t. It would seem like charm, and he didn’t want to charm this girl. He wanted to know her. But the magic of their escape couldn’t extend everywhere.<br>“Maybe I’ll see you in my dreams tonight,” he said instead. “On that road.”<br>Theta’s smile faltered just a bit. “I suppose I’d feel less scared if you were there.”</i><br><b>My heart</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713706.gif" width="340" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and when they did get together, I got so many butterflies in my stomach (that kiss was everything and more):<br><br><i>“It was passionate, yet tender. A mutual agreement of desire. It was a kiss shared. He was kissing <b>her</b>. He was <b>with</b> her.<br>Memphis pulled away. “Everything jake?”<br>“No,” Theta said.<br>“What’s the matter?”<br>Theta looked up at him through thick, dark lashes. “You stopped.”</i><br><br>And not only was Memphis charming and sweet with Theta, he also held his little brother close to heart.<br><br><i>“Good old Memphis. Reliable Memphis. Charming, easygoing Memphis. Look-after-your-brother Memphis. Memphis had been the star once. The miracle man. And it had ended in sorrow. He wouldn’t ever risk that again. These days, he kept his feelings confined to the pages of his notebook.”</i><br><br>The way he watched out and worried about Isaiah pos-i-tute-ly melted my heart.<br><br><i>“Isaiah was all that was left of those happier times when their family was all together, when you only had to walk through the door to hear somebody laughing or calling out, “Who’s that knocking at my door?” and Memphis held tightly to his brother. If anything happened to Isaiah, he wasn’t sure he could survive it.”</i><br>You could tell that he loved his brother <b>fiercely</b>.<br><br>Ahh it's really hard trying to not write whole paragraphs on each character because I loved them all. They had moxie, peculiar powers, and charm. Simply put, they were an enigma that I was dying to solve.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468496887ra/19713707.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And not only were the characters some of the most memorable, but the mystery in the air had me on the edge for nearly the whole book. I also felt so excited whenever little plot points connected throughout the story.<br><br>And can we take a minute to appreciate Miss Lillian and Addie? Because they were such fascinating additions to the ongoing conundrum.<br><br><i>“Miss Addie reached out a finger and slid it over the surface of the half-dollar, paling as she did. “Such a terrible choice to have to make.”<br>“What do you mean?” Evie asked.<br>“Addie sees into the eternal soul,” Miss Lillian said.”</i><br><br>But there are still so many unanswered questions that I'm hoping will be revealed in the next book. Some of my most pressing ones being:<br><br>•The man in the stovepipe.<br>•Louis and Henry.<br>•Project Buffalo.<br>•James.<br>•The girl with the green eyes.<br><br>I feel fully invested in all the characters, and I cannot wait to start <b>Lair of Dreams</b>. Though, I am kind of hesitant because of Jericho and Evie— I'm really not feeling their relationship.<br><br>Oh, and I loved listening to <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=82CdBc0-Umw" rel="nofollow noopener">this song</a> while reading.<br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Diviners</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/031612611X/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=031612611X&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=f63efb1da0a5fd227bc11031449a6c97" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482932148i/21563070.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482932148i/21563071.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Support creators you love.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2241252306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5841660375002696285">I'm obviously late to the party, but I so enjoyed this one! The audiobook took the story to an entirely other level for me; the narrator was fabulous and did so many voices in a unique way without sounding cheesy or lame. Definitely excited to continue on with the series and look forward to answering some of the questions that were left open here. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1892900420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1892900420" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1892900420?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34722429-the-diviners">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mental-illness-disability">mental-illness-disability</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1892900420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13765490172949246792"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She was tired of being told how it was by this generation, who’d botched things so badly. They’d sold their children a pack of lies: God and country. Love your parents. All is fair. And then they’d sent those boys, her brother, off to fight a great monster of a war that maimed and killed and destroyed whatever was inside them. Still they lied, expecting her to mouth the words and play along. Well, she wouldn’t. She knew now that the world was a long way from fair. She knew the monsters w</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13765490172949246792" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>She was tired of being told how it was by this generation, who’d botched things so badly. They’d sold their children a pack of lies: God and country. Love your parents. All is fair. And then they’d sent those boys, her brother, off to fight a great monster of a war that maimed and killed and destroyed whatever was inside them. Still they lied, expecting her to mouth the words and play along. Well, she wouldn’t. She knew now that the world was a long way from fair. She knew the monsters were real.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>I thought once books surpassed 500 pages, they just couldn’t be that exhilarating anymore. I have been proven very, very wrong.</b> Though it's marketed as historical paranormal, I'd classify <i>The Diviners</i> more as a nonstop, action-packed suspense novel. One thing's for sure: <b>this book is nothing like any I've read before.</b> With gorgeous writing, compelling characters, and a creepy plot, <i>The Diviners</i> was so much fun. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>The people made idols and tore them down again, baptizing them in ticker tape parades, blessing them in long tears of profit and loss, throwaway tributes tossed with abandon from tall windows, a celebration of the good times that seem as if they will never stop, the land a fatted calf.</i>
</blockquote><br />What stands out to me when I think about <i>The Diviners</i> is <b>the atmosphere.</b> It's hard to build an unputdownable book out of 570 pages, but this book is so completely engaging. <br /><br />Despite the marketing, <i>The Diviners</i> is not a single pov novel - it follows a cast of characters, all with points of view. There's <b>Evie</b>, a flapper learning to grow up in New York City. <b>Mabel</b>, a loyal friend and source of future character development. <b>Memphis</b>, a black teen trying to deal with his own guilt over his past and protect his brother Isaac. <b>Theta</b>, a kickass and brazen dancer. <b>Henry</b>, her kind piano player roommate and definitely not her boyfriend. <b>Sam</b>, a fuckboy and thief. And <b>Jericho</b>, a very grumpy and very guarded angel. <br /><br />And with all these characters comes a great deal of <b>theme work</b>. With an exploration of racism, generational splits, feminism, and religion, this book is so meaningful. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“There is nothing more terrifying than the absoluteness of one who believes he's right.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I am also, as is usual with first series books, <b>super excited about this story's potential.</b> I'm excited for the <b>found family potential</b> and for <b>all the baited character development.</b> A ton of characters, like Evie and Mabel, are clearly being set up for extensive character arcs. Depending on how I feel about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067572560" rel="nofollow noopener">Lair of Dreams</a>, this might very well turn out to be one of my most recommended books. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13765490172949246792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1216804969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216804969" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216804969?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favs-of-2018">favs-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216804969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8746733794288623668">The best way I can describe this book is The Great Gatsby meets Buzzfeed Unsolved. <br/><br/>Even though this audiobook was 16 hours long, it flew by. I listened to the prologue and had to stop it and take a break because I was already so creeped out, and there were definitely other parts that I read in the middle of the night that made me want to turn my lights on and check under my bed. This book definitely has a creepy vibe and is such an amazing, atmospheric listen. The setting of the 20s was so much </span>
  <span id="freeText8746733794288623668" style="display:none">The best way I can describe this book is The Great Gatsby meets Buzzfeed Unsolved. <br /><br />Even though this audiobook was 16 hours long, it flew by. I listened to the prologue and had to stop it and take a break because I was already so creeped out, and there were definitely other parts that I read in the middle of the night that made me want to turn my lights on and check under my bed. This book definitely has a creepy vibe and is such an amazing, atmospheric listen. The setting of the 20s was so much fun, and I appreciate how Libba took advantage of writing such a diverse cast because NYC was such a melting pot of cultures at that time. <br /><br />However, paranormal thriller just isn't my genre. I'm not well-versed in the thriller genre, but there just seemed to be far too much dramatic irony in this to suspend my attention. We knew more than the characters did, so watching them be like ~omg who did this??~ when we've known for 200 pages was a bit exhausting. Furthermore, knowing that most characters had powers but they were all too scared to tell each other also got pretty old. <br /><br />I originally wanted this to be like Six of Crows where there's a group of people all fighting for one thing, but it was dangerous holding it to that esteem. I liked most of the characters, but they didn't seem quite fleshed out enough to my liking. Also, Evie, the main character, could get pretty tiresome. She had a lot of badass moments, but she could also be impulsive and petty when she was angry, and it made me want to bang my face against a wall. I adore Theta and Henry and Jericho and Sam and Memphis though. <br /><br />I'm really excited to read the sequels but it's gonna have to wait until after Restore Me lol</span>
  <a data-text-id="8746733794288623668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_772944262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772944262" />
    <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772944262?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohammed Arabey" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316126113" href="/book/show/49675850-the-diviners">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772944262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2026255026195860552">..finally released from ‘Starbucks’ before midnight, I was caught in last pages of<b> The Diviners</b>, and heavy rain Storm hit Alexandria that evening.<br/>But as I get off the doors, Everything was different..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386886760ra/7473494.gif' width='500' height='232' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I was facing Alexandria's famous Sea Corniche, cafes' lights, wet streets no more..<br/>There's speakeasy & theater lights instead, the yellow cabs turned into old models..<br/>But the wet streets still there..and The Storm is yet to come..<br/>Well,<b><br/>L-E-T-S--S-T-A-R-T--F-R-O-M--T-H-E--B-E-G-I-N-N-I-N'<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386887588ra/7473816.gif' width='450' height='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481132775i/21390307.jpg' width='360' height='480' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></b><br/>Let's see how</span>
  <span id="freeText2026255026195860552" style="display:none">..finally released from ‘Starbucks’ before midnight, I was caught in last pages of<b> The Diviners</b>, and heavy rain Storm hit Alexandria that evening.<br>But as I get off the doors, Everything was different..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386886760ra/7473494.gif" width="500" height="232" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was facing Alexandria's famous Sea Corniche, cafes' lights, wet streets no more..<br>There's speakeasy &amp; theater lights instead, the yellow cabs turned into old models..<br>But the wet streets still there..and The Storm is yet to come..<br>Well,<b><br>L-E-T-S--S-T-A-R-T--F-R-O-M--T-H-E--B-E-G-I-N-N-I-N'<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386887588ra/7473816.gif" width="450" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481132775i/21390307.jpg" width="360" height="480" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br>Let's see how this elegant Novel, mixed all my favorite Urban Fantasy <b>“Harry Potter”</b>, Paranormal investigation <b>“The X-Files”</b>, and Symbols and Cults ones <b>“Robert Langdon”</b>, Mutants abilities <b>“X-Men”</b>, Creepy Horror <b>“American Horror Story” </b>, New York <b>“666 Park Avenue”</b> and set <b>ALL OF THAT in 1920s atmosphere that <i>literally</i> transferred me from Alexandria, Egypt 2013 to New York, USA 1926.</b><br><blockquote>
<b><u>Day One</u></b> <i>p.59</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481224854i/21401237._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What the Hell ?!! 1926 !!!???<br>The elegant novel I bought cause I liked its cover , I thought will be about Masons because of the Eye symbol.. it turned into social horror set in the 20s.<br><br>Breath..it may be just the beginning .. also don't deny it's interesting with this Ouija board and all, the Jazz music playing constantly in the ‘Starbucks’ cafe helping a bit living it .it'll be alright.<br><br><i>"few pages later"</i><br> WHAT THE F*#^..I MUST do FULL researches for books I'm buying next time..<br>It's all in the 20s, with the Slang that my dictionary won't get..I hate that ..<br><b> Jake, Swell, fella, Pos-i-tute-ly and Blue Noses...</b>Well,<b> BLUE MY SHORTS...-SKI :(</b><br>I spend nearly 4 Hours reading first 35 Pages, to get used to the language..<br><br>And this spoiled <b>Evie</b>, though she has an interesting supernatural talent, yet her attitude is very spoiled.<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481225212i/21401283._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="505" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>I was sooo angry ,too much of <b>Florenz Ziegfeld and Fitzgerald and flapper and fellas ,Revue and Speakeasy </b>(<i>I know I mention the latter at the beginning of the review,but I didn't know this word before</i>) <b>and number runners and gigs!!..</b>what's up with that?<br>I was exhausting with that much of vocabulary and too much similar strange names and slang..<br><br>On the other hand, There's very detailed beautiful drawing for NYC -adorned with the heavy vocabulary- and the atmosphere of the 20s.<br>The characters are very fine detailed too, it reminded me with <b>J.K. Rowling's </b> writing style which I adore...But is the 500+ pages of <b>The Diviners </b>worth this Exhausting Read ?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481225212i/21401284._SX540_.png" width="450" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Day Three</u>
  </b>
  <i> p.154</i>
</blockquote>Well it <i>is</i> worth it indeed..with some search of New York pictures from the 20s -and recently watching Buz Luhrmann's <b>The Great Gatsby</b>- the experience got much better..<br><br>I was already used to the slang and was glad that Mr. Will hates it like me :)<br>Speaking of <b>Mr. Will Fitzgerald</b> , Evie's Uncle ..He reminded me much of <b>Dan Brown's Robert Langdon</b> with all of his knowledge of Occult and Symbols..and the creepy rich supernatural history of US.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481225212i/21401285.jpg" width="450" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He is asked to help solving a mystery of creepy horrible murders...and Evie's special supernatural talent helping him..<br>That's a good story to catch my fully attention.<br><br>And it was getting darker, much complected..<br>It's really worth it..I'm enjoying it so far..<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Day Six</u>
  </b>
  <i> p.275</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481225212ra/21401286.gif" width="450" height="169" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Half way through, <b>It's not a novel..It's a 1920s NYC living experience...</b><br>I became <i> actually, literally</i> living in the 20s' New York.<br>Living in this creepy Bennington Building, going to theaters, watching the motion pictures starring Charlie Chaplin, going to clubs and illegal speakeasy for some shots of giggle water.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481225460ra/21401303.gif" width="450" height="162" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Political groups clashing with the government, wounds aching because the loved one lost to the Great meaningless War..<br>All while investigating horrible crimes with Uncle Will all the same time..<br>Looking for Solomon’s Comet and wondering what is this Coming Storm..<br><br>Nightmares and creepy feelings, Necromancy, Tarot Cards and special Gifts.. a real creepy mix..<br>With some Funny moments that light up the dark a bit…<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386905689i/7477238._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="191" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Amazing Read.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Day Twelve</u>
  </b>
  <i> p.463</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386906247i/7477308._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>“There are doorways between this world and the world of the supernatural. Ghosts. Demonic entities. The unexplained and undefined. The mysterious. I’ve whole books and archives dedicated to it.”<br><br>“There is no greater power on this earth than story.People think boundaries and borders build nations. Nonsense—words do. Beliefs, declarations, constitutions—words. Stories. Myths. Lies. Promises. History.<br>"This, and these..they’re a testament to the country’s rich supernatural history.”</b>
</blockquote><br>It's amazing how big these small words between the Novel’s lines that makes it a real deeper meaning novel.<br><br>There's a great mix of Dark Fantasy and relate it to our Real World "Urban or Contemporary Fantasy”<b><br><br>Religious Movments<br>--------------<blockquote>"Spirits are attracted to seismic energy shifts, chaos and political upheaval, religious movements, war and invention, industry and innovation. There were said to be a great many ghost sightings and unexplained phenomena reported during the American Revolution, and again during the Civil War. This country is founded on a certain tension.”</blockquote></b> <br>And that time, 1920s, with the Great War, the mind-blowing new inventions as electricity and wireless, the religious and politics movements.. All that was a great place to attract spirits.. Specially the Evil ones...<br><i>And talk about the great chaos we're facing in Egypt now..</i><br>And all of that, in a Nation that's built by different believes and religions that can make huger spirits chaos.<br><br>But that's not all,<br><br><b>The Comets<br>--------<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386947633i/7489805._SX540_.jpg" width="449" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>"Comets are powerful portents! The ancients believed them to be times when the veil between this world and the next was thinnest."</blockquote></b>Well that last one freaks me out since I was reading other Arabic novel about a theory similar to that, the relation between Comets and Evil Demons which is even mentioned at the Holy Qura'an.<br><br>Again, that's not all the creep you'd get here. The Novel is Getting Darker...<br><b>Full with Supernatural and Metaphysics, Amazingly describing the Nightmares and the creepy atmosphere of the time, </b>like The two old creepy ladies at the building, the graveyards, the abounded house, Chinatown and the hostess girl in green eyes..the creepy festival..<b>and so more..more real..<br><br>That Eugenics Test with the creepy enthusiastic nurse.</b><br> <i>-and as I felt about it, THAT was real, the author said so at the notes, and google it, it's there</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386949322i/7490175._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="288" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386949322i/7490176._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="355" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That reminded me with the best element of <b>X-Men</b> with all the diviners -mutants- investigations, the rejection and considering them "freaks".. all the like of <b>Harry Potter</b> as well.<br><br>Also the part with<b> The Brethren </b>place, their church and community reminded me with an episode of <b>The X-Files</b> that hunts me years before.<br><br>All that tangled with The REAL 1920s New York. <i>in a way the author called ‘<b>Narrative Tinkering</b>’</i><br>That reminds me of why I love that color of fantasy that I got in love with because of <b>Harry Potter </b>... and this symbols biblical killer chase like <b>Robert Langdon</b>'s adventures...and nice vast variety of sweet characters that you'd feel as if you're living with them, sometimes cracked me up with laughter,<b>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481225718i/21401325._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="282" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <blockquote>“To Mabel! You could at least try to be polite.”<br>“I’m not interested in being polite. It’s false. Nietzsche says—”<br>“Leave Nietzsche out of this. He’s dead, and for all I know he died of rudeness.” Evie fumed.</blockquote>
</b><br>I simply loved it..if you sum up you'll find it gets the best elements of EVERYTHING I love in fictions and Horror..<b>"Harry Potter" , "The X-Files" , "Dan Brown's Robert Langdon" , "X-Men" , " 666 Park Avenue" </b>even the great horror show<b> "American Horror Story"<br><br>So I have to Thank you Libba Bray for the cinematic, living characters and places.. your describing the Evie's ‘Trance State’ when she holds something to read, is exactly like describing my actual state of reading...when I read a good novel I'm actually living and seeing it , the atmosphere and the cast I choose for the characters.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386951513i/7491146._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And here I am, 12 days living there...New York 1926</b><br><br><blockquote>
<b><u>Day Fifteen</u></b> <i>"Last Day" p.578</i>
</blockquote><br>With no spoilers..That's a very good climax, yet, I was shocked…it didn't end.<br>About 40% of the book and may be more is a base for the upcoming volume and not direct related to this one's mystery.<br><br>Is it bad surprise? <i>Never</i> <b> It's still amazing and thrilled me, Now I want more volumes, even more than a trilogy, why not a 7 parts like Harry?<br>Want more stories of the characters I loved , the creepiest events And the Howling Storm that yet to come.<br>Libby made a great base that she can build a wonderful series that can get its place at the Biggest Fiction Series Ever Made.<br></b><br>The Ending Scene gave me a real Nightmare I add at the 2nd book Pre-Review :)<br><br><b>
  <u>The God</u>
</b><br>---------<br>One important note before I wrap up..it may disturbed me a bit all the anti-God talks in the novel..<br>BUT at the same time I feel the series got something Good about God after all..I may can't put finger on it but it's there...I felt it in Memphis' pray for his brother by the end..<br>A Line by the end shows that usually our choices that get wrong..not all the wrong is just from God..<br><blockquote>“Memphis John, you need to get beside me. We’re gonna pray for your brother now, pray the woman hasn’t brought the Devil to this house.”<br>Memphis dropped to his knees next to his aunt at Isaiah’s bedside, but he didn’t like it. Why? he thought. Why should I pray to God? What has he done for me or my family? He felt the anger coming up inside, pricking into tears.<br>“I won’t do it.” Octavia’s shock faded to a grim determination. “I promised your mama I would look after her boys, and I intend to do that. Now pray with me.”<br>Memphis exploded. “Why don’t you ask God why he took my mother? Why don’t you ask him when my father’s coming home? Why don’t you ask him what he has against my little brother?” He wanted to hit something or someone. He wanted to burn up the whole world, heal it, and burn it down again.<br>He expected Octavia to yell at him for blaspheming the Lord and throw him out of the house. Instead, she said softly, “Go on and get yourself some chicken from the icebox. I’ll do the praying, and we’ll talk after,” and it was almost worse. Octavia bowed her head. “Lord Jesus… please protect this boy. He didn’t know what he was doing. He’s a good boy, Jesus…” </blockquote><br>But this part show may be a little hidden better idea.<br><blockquote>“Thank you,” he said, though he didn’t know who he was saying it to, or why.</blockquote><br>I don't know but I got a good felling about it after all..I loved also this part about how wrong the man can be.. that we who choose the wrong , every time..<b><br><blockquote>Will wanted her to go inside. Then he would send her back to Ohio, where her parents would also tell her to go inside, in effect. She was tired of being told how it was by this generation, who’d botched things so badly. They’d sold their children a pack of lies: God and country. Love your parents. All is fair. And then they’d sent those boys, her brother, off to fight a great monster of a war that maimed and killed and destroyed whatever was inside them. Still they lied, expecting her to mouth the words and play along. Well, she wouldn’t. She knew now that the world was a long way from fair. She knew the monsters were real.</blockquote>
<br><br>I closed the book...and went out off the Starbucks cafe, real rain storm hit Alexandria on the eve of 11/12/13...But I’m seeing it hitting Manhattan streets since I'm still in the trance of The Diviners..A Novel, An Experience that was beyond words and reviews...an amazing reading..A real Living story..exhausting, yes, but Pos-i-tute-ly wonderful one-ski..Swell Read :)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386953180ra/7491641.gif" width="450" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><br> Mohammed Arabey<br>From 24th November 2013<br>To 11 December 2013<br></b><i><br><br>PS: The Facebook page really helpful with Pictures and advertising from the 20s ,even Naughty John's horrible tune..as well as the official website..It's really Swell :)<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/TheDivinersSeries">https://www.facebook.com/TheDivinersS...</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2026255026195860552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

She grated on my nerves so badly, I can barely bring myself to read on. I find Libba Bray's writing style for this book completely unreadable. I have a strong suspicion she read a reference guide to using slang during the Flapper era and made it her personal goal to use as much speakeasy language as possible in every single spoken sentence.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042791916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7175928952739532707">This was my third attempt at this book and... victory at last!<br/><br/>Once again it was a rather slow start that failed to grip me mind body and soul right from the get-go (that might’ve been too much to ask. Hence the third attempt) but once I passed that difficult stage, I found it enjoyable. <br/>I wouldn’t go so far as to say extremely enjoyable but I was hooked nonetheless. <br/><br/>The plot was extremely well written and the history elements were amazingly researched and in-depth. <br/>My initial reason to give this</span>
  <span id="freeText7175928952739532707" style="display:none">This was my third attempt at this book and... victory at last!<br /><br />Once again it was a rather slow start that failed to grip me mind body and soul right from the get-go (that might’ve been too much to ask. Hence the third attempt) but once I passed that difficult stage, I found it enjoyable. <br />I wouldn’t go so far as to say extremely enjoyable but I was hooked nonetheless. <br /><br />The plot was extremely well written and the history elements were amazingly researched and in-depth. <br />My initial reason to give this another try was because I needed a chilling read that’d give me goosebumps or something along that line and, again, that too was too much to ask, ‘cause although it was creepy and relatively disturbing, it didn’t end up being the bone-chilling read I suspected and was in desperate mood for. <br /><br />The best part, after the history lesson, so to speak, were the refreshingly different characters that graced this novel. <br />It had a rich variety of individual characters who were (almost) all vividly depicted. Apart from one, that is. 🤦‍♀️<br /><br />*Long Sigh* <br />That’s where our “lovely” heroine, Evie O’Neil comes in. The childish and “rebellious” MC with her painfully annoying slangs and over the top perkiness that I just found too too too annoying!!<br />She was selfish, desperate for attention, so desperate that even she was aware of it, though she wore it like a badge of honour, and so utterly exasperating to the point where I genuinely started dreading coming to her parts because I couldn’t take it anymore. <br />I hated the unnecessary excess charm and those slangs she used every time she spoke. Those slangs!!!<br />Mostly I was just like, for the love of all that is good, please do be quite and let the grownups talk! 🤦‍♀️ I found her too much to bear. I DID NOT LIKE HER. NOT ONE BIT. <br /><br />All in all, it was a fun read that didn’t quite hit the mark but fun nonetheless. The 1920s Manhattan setting was great and the villain of the book, Naughty John definitely made this an overall entertaining read. <br /><br />A part of me wants to get through this series and see where it goes but if I don’t, it’ll most probably be because of Evie. <br />I don’t think I can take anymore of her. Maybe if I take a long enough break in between, I’ll forget how infuriatingly irritating she is. Unlikely but... one hopes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7175928952739532707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2137918439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137918439" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137918439?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316232425" href="/book/show/15927006-the-diviners">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=physical-shelf">physical-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=05-stars">05-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137918439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12232566045644217684">New favorite obsession! It’s dark but classy...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292855.gif' alt='' width='350' height='147' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>...beautiful but swallowed in the feel of a haunting. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292852.gif' alt='' width='350' height='145' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There are a lot of characters in this book. So, let’s do this list style:<br/><br/><u>Evie O'Neill</u><br/>I <i>positutely</i> love Evie. She is such a unique heroine. Usually, the heroines these days are mysterious, introverted and quiet about how they are different. Evie is none of those things. She is a flapper (setting is in the 1920s), she is as extroverted and confident as they come, and she isn’t shy about what she ca</span>
  <span id="freeText12232566045644217684" style="display:none">New favorite obsession! It’s dark but classy...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292855.gif" alt="" width="350" height="147" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...beautiful but swallowed in the feel of a haunting. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292852.gif" alt="" width="350" height="145" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are a lot of characters in this book. So, let’s do this list style:<br><br><u>Evie O'Neill</u><br>I <i>positutely</i> love Evie. She is such a unique heroine. Usually, the heroines these days are mysterious, introverted and quiet about how they are different. Evie is none of those things. She is a flapper (setting is in the 1920s), she is as extroverted and confident as they come, and she isn’t shy about what she can do.<br><br>If you give her an object, <i>any old thing</i>, she can tell you some things about yourself. Vague things like what you ate for breakfast or where you went that day, or she can learn the desires of your heart if she tries hard enough. She uses this as a party gag and plays it off like it’s a trick. Hiding in plain sight, you see. She’s brilliant. <br><br><u>Mabel Rose</u><br>When Evie gets sent to live with her Uncle in New York, she is happy to be reunited with one of her old pals Mabel. Mabel kind of does whatever Evie tells her to do, and she has helicopter parents, but she doesn’t mind the adventure that comes with being friends with Evie. Oh, and she has a major crush on the gentlemen who works with Evie’s uncle, Jericho. <br><br><u>Will Fitzgerald</u><br>This is Evie’s Uncle, or “<i>Unc</i>” as she calls him. He runs <b>The Museum of American Folklore, Superstition, and the Occult</b>, or as locals call it, <b>The Museum of the Creepy Crawlies</b>. He teaches classes to gentlemen here and there, but the museum itself is not doing too well. Evie is fixin’ to change that for him though. He has a lot of secrets that aren’t even fully revealed in this book, so I am eager to know more about his past.<br><br><u>Sam Lloyd / Sergei Lubovitch</u><br>He gets on Evie’s last nerve (he owes her twenty dollars!). He literally runs into Evie on her way to her Unc’s and pick-pocketed her. So, when she saw him again, she was all about ruining any chances he got to do it again <b>and she just wants her money back</b>. He is a very talented liar, thief and all-around smooth talker. He also has a few tricks up his sleeves…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292853.gif" alt="" width="350" height="145" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Jericho Jones</u><br>Jericho is a big, strong young man who works with Will Fitzgerald at The Museum of the Creepy Crawlies. He’s quiet but doesn’t let people walk on him. He has a big secret revealed towards the end that makes me feel as if this as some steam-punk sprinkled into the genre. <br><br><u>Memphis Campbell</u><br>Memphis used to have a power like Evie’s. He could heal people with the touch of his hands. But after a series of unfortunate event (<i>I love that phrase</i>), he no longer can channel that part of him. His story doesn’t really touch with the five above. In some parts he meets some of them, but he has his own story line going on. He’s African American, so you see a lot of the horrible ways people of the same race were treated back in the day. Memphis little brother, Isaiah Campbell, has a power of his own as well. <br><br><u>Theta Knight</u><br>She is a Ziegfeld girl and a friend of Evie’s. She actually becomes the chain between Memphis and the rest of the group. She meets him and they have a little, casual attraction between the two after they realize they are having the same dream. I am loving this checker-board love. I can see there is going to be a lot of problems with this in the future, but I absolutely am sailing this ship into the sunset. <br><br>Theta has a dark past. She, as well, has a little magic in her… but it gets her in all kinds of trouble and she has been on the run ever since. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292854.gif" alt="" width="350" height="145" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Henry DuBois</u><br>We don’t know much about him other than he likes men, may have a trick up his sleeve, and a huge heart for his now-roommate Theta Knight. Without him, Theta would be in a whole other type of situation. I hear we get a lot more of him in the next book though, so I am anxious to read it.<br><br><u>Naughty John</u><br>This is our antagonist. Like I’m going to tell you anything about him besides he is messed up in the head and he needs the actual Lord and not the Lord he thinks he knows.<br><br>There are other characters that play a big part even though they aren’t mentioned as often, like <b>Blind Bill Johnson</b> who has a power of his own, <b>The Proctor Sisters</b> who seem to know a lot about magic and what is to come, a gentleman named <b>Arthur</b> who seems to be too interested in Mabel, a crow that keeps bothering Memphis, and a girl with green eyes.<br><br><b>SO WHAT IS THIS STORY ACTUALLY ABOUT?</b><br>Young adults finding out why they have some supernatural power and murders… lots and lots of murders… and ghost… and murders… murders… <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509117702ra/24292856.gif" alt="" width="350" height="155" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is so well rounded and the setting is absolutely to die for. I love the twenties (cliché, I know); but, what I love more is creep. I love the creepiness of this book. Any book that makes my skin crawl is a book I am going to hold onto for the rest of my life. <br><br>Warning that there is an actual love-triangle forming and I have the ships that I am sailing and I will riot if I don’t get my way.<br><br>And sweetie, <b>please listen to this book</b>. I don’t care if you read along with the narrator or if you just listen to it while you drive. <b>January LaVoy is one of the best narrators I have ever listened to</b>. I will forever be on the lookout for books she narrates. <br><br><b>
  <u>This is really where my review ends. Below is a rant, so proceed at your own risk.</u>
</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I do have… one problem with this book. Literally one. The rest of this book is golden and it will be in the lead of my favorite books for the rest of my life. <br><br><b>Representation.</b> Libra Bray has always been phenomenal at making sure everyone can relate to someone. I look to her when someone talks about representation. With that being said, I don’t know how to go about this without getting my ear chewed off by some angry commenter or without offending the author who lead the way for me to become a reader. So, please know this is something I feel strongly towards because it is a big part of my life. Know that I am not meaning to offend anyone and that I just want to be heard. You don’t have to understand where I am coming from, <u>but you do need to respect my words, just like I would respect your words</u>. This means <b>do not attack me, please. We can have a friendly conversation about it, but I will not be responding to attacks.</b><br><br>Where is the representation of <b>sane</b> Christians? They are either crazy and shoving a Bible in your face, controlling and twisting the words in the Bible, or they are literally mentally insane and using the religion as an excuse for what they are doing. There are literally at least one of each of these types of characters in this book, but none with a level, easy-going head. And I know, you can’t represent every-kind of person in the world in one book. I completely understand that, as to how I am writing a book of my own, but I feel <i>if you are going to shove one type of person in such a bad light with three characters, shouldn’t you have at least one character who is in a better light?</i><br><br>I am a strong Christian. I pride myself on that. I know it isn’t the popular thing in our day and age and people may pre-judge me or unfriend me because I call myself a Christian. But please hear me: <b>I am an accepting Christian</b>. I don’t care what other people do to themselves or to their lives (<i>as long as no one is hurt, everyone is of age and everyone involved is consensual</i>) because that is how <b>they want to live</b>. If they ask me about my faith, sure we can talk about it, but I am not going to shove my beliefs at someone <b>because when on earth did that actually work?</b><br><br>There are a lot of Christians like this. The ones in the media (books, TV shows, movies) are literally the minority. <b>So I am not just picking on the lovely Libba Bray who I admire so much as a writer, story teller and just as a person in general</b>. Christians are always portrayed as crazy and controlling in the media, when I’m over here watching Game of Thrones and planning next week’s devotional. I’m reading risky books and listening to praise and worship music. I have an obsession, <i>which is probably a super unhealthy obsession but let’s not get into that</i>, with Harry Potter and an equally-unhealth obsession with any Francine Rivers’ books. <br><br>I’m just ranting at this point, but hear this: I am a strong, accepting, level-headed Christian with friends of all religions and faiths and I love them for who they are and who they want to be just as they love me for who I am and who I am trying to be. <br><br><b>Where’s my representation?</b>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I loved this book. I’m going to love the series. I love the Gemma Doyle series. I love this author. Libba Bray is who I aspire to be like. I need more people to read this so I can fan-girl with them.<br><br>---<br><br>This was positutely the best creepy yet classy and well rounded story I’ve read in my whole entire life. RTC. <br><br>- - - <br><br>More than half way through and not sure if I’m going to jump into the air with glee or start digging a 6 foot deep hole when I’m finished with it. <br><br>- - -<br><br>Um... this is amazing. It’s just the right amount of class and creep. Why isn’t this talked about more?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2568295163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568295163" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568295163?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568295163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6271748833514544859">You have no idea how many times I have wanted to be able to mark this book as ‘‘read’’ on Goodreads. The first time I attempted to read it, I was only 16 and gave up after the first two chapters. Then I tried again a few years ago but gave up at page 50. But something in me really wanted to finish this book, whether I ended up loving it or hating it, so I finally decided to sit somewhere quiet and immerse myself in this story a month ago.<br/><br/>The reason why I couldn’t finish it those two previous tim</span>
  <span id="freeText6271748833514544859" style="display:none">You have no idea how many times I have wanted to be able to mark this book as ‘‘read’’ on Goodreads. The first time I attempted to read it, I was only 16 and gave up after the first two chapters. Then I tried again a few years ago but gave up at page 50. But something in me really wanted to finish this book, whether I ended up loving it or hating it, so I finally decided to sit somewhere quiet and immerse myself in this story a month ago.<br /><br />The reason why I couldn’t finish it those two previous times is that this is a historical fiction story, and although there are fantasy elements, it FEELS historical and the characters use language that confused me at times. At 16, I just could not deal with the 1920s New York expressions that simply did not make sense to me. Also, I did not manage to connect with Evie—one of the main characters.<br /><br />But the thing about Evie is that she grows on you. Yes, she is spoiled and would rather party than work hard (which, to think of it, makes sense), but the more you read about her, the more you’re able to sympathize with her and understand why she prefers to dwell on light topics than serious ones. She lost her brother. She keeps important secrets. She feels alone, misunderstood, haunted. Honestly, after the narrator became more open with us regarding her, I began to admire her happy-go-lucky demeanour. It’s not easy to be happy when there is so much to be sad about. <br /><br />I understand why so many people were not able to finish this book, clearly. But I also understand all of those who loved it so much. It’s different from literally anything I have read before and there is a lot of content. Many 400+ page books feel like they barely tell a story or they barely show anything new, but this is quite an original work that must have taken the author a long time to write. It most definitely feels as though she thought it out carefully and wanted from it so much. I do dare say Libba Bray has accomplished something worth praising here. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6271748833514544859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2315941947" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315941947" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315941947?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
